yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	28	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	29	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	11	0.1

Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	3	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	25	0.1

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	31	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	29	0.1

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	12	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	24	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	9	0.1

Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	2	0.1

A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Tetrad Two Gene Distance</h6><p>The yeast <i>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> has unordered tetrads. A cross is made to study the linkage relationships among two genes. <p>Using the table above, determine the distance between the two genes.</p> <ul> <li><i>Hint 1:</i> The gene distance will be a whole number, do NOT enter a decimal; if you have a decimal your calculations are likely wrong.</li><li><i>Hint 2:</i> enter your answer in the blank using only numbers  with no spaces or commas. Also, do NOT add units, e.g. cM or m.u.</li></ul> <p>Dr. Voss guide to unordered tetrads:</p><ul><li>Step 1: Find the Row for the Parental Ditype (PD).</li><li>Step 2: Assign PD, NPD, TT for each row</li><li>Step 3: Determine if the two genes are linked.</li><ul><li>PD >> NPD &rarr; linked; PD &approx; NPD &rarr; unlinked</li></ul><li>Step 4: Determine the map distance between the two genes</li><ul><li>D = &half; (TT + 6 NPD)/total = (3 NPD + &half;TT)/total</li></ul></ul>	18	0.1
